Zhenjiang 98

Public Buses are Destroyed In order to facilitate the people's travel, the Jiangsu Construction Department is piloting public buses in the provincial capital. Unexpectedly, they were destroyed on the first day of operation. At 9:45 a.m. on the 22nd, a public bus with the number 0822 drove out of the Provincial Government Road. When it reached the intersection of the station road, the rickshaw pullers in the city believed that the construction department was driving public buses in the city and that the livelihood of the rickshaw pullers would be taken away. They gathered two or three hundred rickshaw pullers and waited in advance. When they saw the bus coming, they swarmed forward and used stones to destroy it. They destroyed all the machines and glass. The bus drivers were also beaten. They immediately reported to the second police station stationed at the station. The patrol captain of the station led the police to suppress the incident and took the rickshaw pullers Qian Zhonghong, Yu Junsheng, and Tang Dazhong to the station. When the rickshaw pullers saw that Qian and others were detained, they also swarmed to the station, and the order was in chaos for a while. At that time, two railway workers, Lu Hengzhi and Cui Yunlong, passed by. The police officers at the station mistakenly thought they were the rickshaw pullers who caused the trouble and went forward to arrest them. Lu and others believed that they were arrested innocently and resisted, resulting in a conflict. The two workers were injured in the waist. The station police department sent the workers to the railway hospital for treatment. The arrested rickshaw pullers were sent to the fifth branch for interrogation.

The Provincial Government Jointly Tries Two County Magistrates Peng Guoyan, the magistrate of Pi County, and Hong Fuyuan, the magistrate of Funing County, were detained by Zhao, the director of the Civil Affairs Department, in the provincial capital on the 6th of this month and held in the provincial capital's Public Security Bureau for a long time. It is now known that Chairman Gu Zhutong, Zhao Qilu, the director of the Civil Affairs Department, He Yushu, the director of the Industry Department, Shu Shifu, the director of the Finance Department, and Dong Xiujia, the director of the Construction Department, ordered the police of the provincial capital's Public Security Bureau to escort Peng and Hong to the government the day before yesterday. In the ordinary conference room, they were interrogated one by one according to the accusations. After more than an hour, Chairman Gu personally ordered Peng and Hong to be returned to the custody of the police of the provincial capital's Public Security Bureau.

Jiaxing 99

Relief for the Silk Cocoon Market: The silkworm season in Jiaxing is approaching its peak, and large-scale silkworm rearing is coming to an end. A banking syndicate has specially raised 600,000 yuan in cash to meet the needs of cocoon merchants. The provincial government, also aiming to relieve the cocoon market, has negotiated with the banking syndicate to establish a Cocoon Market Relief Committee, raising 1.8 million yuan for cocoon merchants in various counties to borrow. However, many cocoon merchants remain hesitant, unwilling to borrow to purchase cocoons. Yesterday, key figures from the Cocoon Industry Association, including Zhang Ximin, Cha Shuxiang, Wu Heshu, and Shen Yijun, proposed establishing a cocoon-drying factory in each of the seven districts of the county for the convenience of farmers. Each factory would cost approximately 2,000 yuan, totaling 14,000 yuan, to be borrowed from local public funds and repaid after the silkworm season. Drying prices are yet to be determined; cocoons would be temporarily stored, and after their future sale, the remaining funds, after deducting all expenses, would be returned to the cocoon owners. Regulations for cocoon drying and consignment sales are currently being drafted and will be submitted to the provincial government for approval before implementation.

County Magistrate Gong's Resignation Approved: Jiaxing County Magistrate Gong Shinong has resigned from his position due to the difficulty of handling affairs. His resignation has been approved by the provincial government. The provincial government has approved Jiang Ruo as his replacement.

Shaoxing 100

Detective Conflict with Local Militia: Recently, banditry has been rampant in the rural areas of Shaoxing. The detective squad dispatched several undercover agents to investigate separately. On the 21st, they apprehended two bandits, Tong Asi and Zhao Alai, who was piloting the bandits' boat, in the Ma'an area. They confessed to their accomplices, and the detectives were preparing to apprehend other bandits when Zhao Yusheng, the town leader of the area, intervened on behalf of Zhao Alai because of kinship. He requested the release of Zhao Alai, but the detectives refused. Zhao Yusheng then ordered the local militia to confront the detectives with guns, attempting to seize their weapons, leading to a conflict that nearly resulted in gunfire. Fortunately, Squad Leader Zhou arrived and ordered the militia to disperse, resolving the situation. The detectives have now submitted evidence of the case and the resistance to arrest to the Public Security Bureau and the county government for investigation.

Apprentice in Wuzhou Pharmacy Commits Suicide by Poisoning: Qiu Yinsheng, an apprentice at the Wuzhou Pharmacy on Shaoxing Main Street, was in his twenties and had previously worked as a teacher at a certain school. Feeling the hardship of the teaching profession, he abandoned his studies and became a merchant apprentice at the pharmacy. He was known for his diligence and conscientiousness. On the evening of the 22nd of this month, he had a minor argument with a colleague, which was resolved after mediation, and everyone went to sleep. Unexpectedly, the apprentice secretly took sleeping pills and morphine sold in the pharmacy during the night and ingested them, committing suicide. He was discovered the next morning and rushed to the hospital for treatment. However, due to the excessive amount of poison ingested, he could not be saved and tragically died.

Xiaoshan 101

Damage from Heavy Rainfall: Since the 20th of this month, Xiaoshan has been experiencing torrential rains, causing river water levels to rise by over ten feet within a day and night. The water level in the plains reached several inches, allowing boats to navigate through the main streets and alleys. Broad beans and wheat in the countryside have been submerged, resulting in immeasurable losses for farmers. Collapsed houses and walls are a common sight in the town. The weather remains adverse and oppressively hot, with continued signs of rain. If the weather does not clear soon, the rural areas will be devastated by flooding, and the spring harvest will be completely hopeless.

Pan Youxiang's Murder of Her Husband: Fu, the wife of peasant Cao Guisheng from Pan Youxiang outside the South Gate of Xiaoshan, had been having an affair for some time and viewed her husband as a thorn in her side. On the night of the 21st, she colluded with her lover to murder her husband, Cao Guisheng, by first cutting off his tongue with a sharp knife and then crushing his testicles. The incident was discovered by the local police, who reported it to the county for investigation. The county government dispatched several police officers to investigate and arrested both the adulterer and adulteress for interrogation.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce's Letter to Foreign Chambers of Commerce

Refuting the Absurdity of a Free City 105

Japanese Mislead the British Residents Association

Safety of Commercial Cities Based on Fairness and Justice

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the foreign chambers of commerce in Shanghai yesterday, refuting the British Residents Association's absurd notion of supporting a free city. The original letter reads: Dear Sirs, We have seen in the newspapers that the British Residents Association has sent a letter to the various foreign chambers of commerce, requesting their support for the following resolutions and expressing their views to the Chinese government, strongly advocating the necessity of convening a roundtable conference so that the major powers of the world can discuss these and other issues. Our chamber has reviewed the attached resolutions, which identify the causes of recent conflicts and disputes as: (1) The extraterritoriality courts; (2) The administrative rights over roads built outside the settlements; (3) The presence of armed troops in and around Shanghai. It claims that unless the above outstanding issues are resolved simultaneously, the recent Sino-Japanese dispute in Shanghai cannot be permanently and satisfactorily resolved. Our chamber believes that such a statement in the resolutions of an association is quite shocking. In terms of diplomatic relations, the United Kingdom is a friendly nation to both China and Japan, and there is no reason to exclusively cater to the satisfaction of one side. If only the satisfaction of Japan is considered, the Sino-Japanese dispute will be hidden and will inevitably become more prolonged and lead to more severe disasters. In terms of commercial relations, such important issues should take into account the public opinion of the merchants residing in the country. Why was consent never sought in advance, and instead, Japan's intentions and interests were followed? What is the public opinion of the merchants residing in the country? In February of this year, when the Japanese military invasion of Shanghai was at its peak, officials from the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs proposed designating Tianjin, Qingdao, Hankou, Shanghai, and Guangzhou as free cities where no Chinese troops would be stationed forever, hoping to gauge international public opinion. At that time, our chamber issued a declaration, strongly refuting it, stating that the deployment of troops by a country cannot be subject to the interference of other countries. Most countries also scoffed at the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs' proposal. As a result, the Japanese side then disavowed this opinion, claiming that it was merely a private proposal by the official. From this perspective, the free city of Shanghai advocated by Japan today is merely a scene in a drama from that time. Japan's advocacy of a free city of Shanghai has two intentions: (1) Since the three northeastern provinces have already been monopolized by them, and the commerce of various countries in the three northeastern provinces has plummeted, they want to use this as a place to offer favors; (2) The Songhu war has lasted for several months, and the commerce of various countries in Shanghai has suffered greatly. They want to use this to ingratiate themselves with the various countries as a means of self-redemption. Here, our chamber dares to faithfully advise our friendly nations that the foreign merchants in China hope for the advancement of commerce and the safety of the commercial city of Shanghai, which is a common desire and a common principle. However, it must be based on fairness and justice and not seek other strategies. The goodwill of 400 million people is the most effective salesman for goods in China and the safest fortress to protect the commercial city of Shanghai. Since Japan forcibly occupied Shenyang, the commerce of various countries with China has suddenly increased compared to before. This fact is clearly evident. Japan, unable to suppress its jealousy, has proposed the free city in the hope that the various countries will initiate negotiations in order to secretly sow discord. Why? Because Japan forcibly seized our three northeastern provinces and restricted our sovereignty in Shanghai, it is naturally resented by the Chinese people. However, the matter of the three northeastern provinces was created entirely by Japan. The proposal for a free city of Shanghai was initiated by Japan first, and the various countries followed after. The Chinese people will inevitably transfer their resentment towards Japan to the various countries. This is the first step in the success of Japan's diplomatic policy, and the British Residents Association has also been misled. The cause of the outbreak of the Songhu war this time (1) can be said to be due to the Japanese naval officers' ambition to follow in the footsteps of the army warlords and make Shanghai their place of conquest. This is evident from the repeated informal declarations of the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs, which stated that the Shanghai incident was left to the discretion of naval personnel. The truth of the incident is thus proven. (2) Since they have made the three northeastern provinces their lifeline, they also want to control the commercial arteries of the Yangtze River as their source of sustenance. However, Shanghai does not have a Japanese-controlled settlement that can be used as a base, so they want to take this opportunity to create one. In analysis, the motivation for the war on that day was nothing more than this. Therefore, the garrisoning of troops in Shanghai is by no means the real cause of the outbreak of the war. In terms of boycotts, Shanghai has had nine such boycotts against Japan. In terms of troop deployments, the presence of Chinese troops around Shanghai has been a long-standing phenomenon and did not start last year. Why has there been peace all along, but this time it suddenly erupted? Therefore, upon investigation, the three issues listed by the British Residents Association are not related to the Sino-Japanese conflict in Shanghai. As for the roads outside the settlements and the extraterritoriality courts, they are even less relevant to Japan. Japanese newspapers have never paid attention to this. If the various friendly nations want to ensure the safety of their commerce with China, they should first assist China in achieving a satisfactory resolution to the three northeastern provinces incident. Then all Sino-Japanese conflicts will naturally be eliminated. Not only will the peace and order of Shanghai be preserved, but the entire commerce with China will also increase. If this cannot be achieved for the time being, they should also exercise keen observation in every matter, stand in an impartial position, and not be dazzled by Japan's false words. It should be noted that Shanghai underwent 34 days of intense fighting this time, but the Chinese troops never entered the settlements. Even when Japan used the settlements as a base, the Chinese troops did not pursue them. Therefore, to ensure the safety of the settlements this time, only a real guarantee needs to be sought from Japan. Instead of doing this, they want to limit the deployment of Chinese troops. Such an unfair and unjust approach is naturally unacceptable to our country. Why do the various friendly nations abandon their goodwill towards China and share the blame for Japan? Therefore, the resolutions of the British Residents Association, from the perspective of the commerce of various countries with China, should not be easily supported. Our chamber dares to represent the Chinese merchants of the entire city and offer its sincere advice. We hope you will take it into consideration.

The Japanese Ministry of the Navy urgently dispatched the warship Ryuta to Shanghai yesterday to transport Shirakawa's body back to Japan. Jiejiang Company

Yiling Sinks After Striking Reef 107

Accident in Yangduxi

Completely Submerged Within Twenty Minutes

All Passengers and Crew Drowned

The American Jiejiang Company's Yiling轮, en route from Chongqing to Shanghai, struck a reef between Wanxian and Yichang. The ship sank completely within twenty minutes, resulting in numerous passenger and crew deaths. Our reporter conducted an investigation, and the details are as follows:

Circumstances of the Accident: The Yiling轮, carrying cargo and over forty passengers from Chongqing to Shanghai, departed Chongqing on the 23rd. At noon on the 25th, it was sailing on the Yangtze River between Yichang downstream and Wanxian upstream, in an area called Yangduxi. This area is known for its numerous reefs, making it one of the most difficult stretches for ships to navigate. Recently, the water level of the upper Yangtze River has been fluctuating sharply. The submerged reefs in this area are exposed when the water is low, allowing ships to avoid them. However, due to the rising water, the reefs were submerged, making them invisible to passing ships. The Yiling轮 was sailing downstream when the turbulent waters pushed it onto a submerged reef. The ship's hull was breached by the reef, causing it to immediately take on water and sink.

Rapid Sinking: According to reports, the Yiling轮's accident was caused by the ship's hull colliding with a reef due to the turbulent downstream current. The impact was so severe that the hull immediately broke, and the rushing river water caused the ship to sink within a matter of moments. The ship was completely submerged in the river within just twenty minutes, with only a section of the mast visible. According to sources within the company, the accident was caused by (1) the fluctuating water levels of the river and (2) the pilot's error in guiding the ship, causing it to strike the reef.

Personnel Casualties: It is reported that there were a total of forty-five passengers on board, along with over ten crew members, including sailors and stokers. When the ship struck the reef, the entire ship shook. Passengers in the cabins were trying to escape, and crew members and sailors on deck were trying to release lifeboats and life jackets. However, due to the rapid sinking, they were unable to escape. All passengers and crew were drowned with the ship, resulting in an unprecedented tragedy.

Shipowner Escapes Danger: Yesterday morning, the Jiejiang Company received a radio report from an American warship in Yangduxi regarding the Yiling轮's accident, stating that the shipowner, Mr. Haenesson, had been rescued and was being transported to Chongqing on the Yujiang轮, which was sailing upstream. Most of the other passengers and crew who fell into the water had been swept away by the turbulent currents or died inside the ship. Only about two or three people were able to escape after falling into the water. Detailed information has not yet been reported to Shanghai. The Shanghai office sent a telegram to Chongqing yesterday to inquire and ordered the salvage and rescue of the passengers who fell into the water.

Ship Loss: Among the Jiejiang Company's Yangtze River ships, the Yiling轮 was the best. It had a displacement of 300 tons, an iron hull, and an excellent engine. It had been navigating the Sichuan River for over ten years and had never run aground or had an accident. It was one of the most perfect ships on the Yangtze River. This time, it was sailing downstream from Chongqing with relatively little cargo. Now, including the mail, everything has been lost, resulting in losses of at least 100,000 yuan.

Detain American Over Minor Incident 110

According to the North China Daily News, yesterday (26th), there were reports of Japanese troops mistreating an American citizen to the US Consulate. It is alleged that on Monday afternoon at approximately 1:45 PM, Mr. Steiz, an American citizen from the Victor Company, along with Mr. Hand and a Briton, Mr. Glover, were driving east along Pingliang Road when a Japanese naval vehicle sped towards them, nearly forcing them off the road. Mr. Steiz informed them that they were driving recklessly and almost caused an accident. He arrived at the bureau at 10:10 AM to take office. The Director of the Public Utilities Bureau, Huang Boqiao, the Director of the Public Works Bureau, Shen Yi, the Director of the Education Bureau, Xu Peihuang, the Director of the Health Bureau, Hu Hongji, Wang Yansong from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Pan Gongzhan from the Municipal Party Headquarters, and representatives from various sectors all came to the bureau to offer their congratulations.

Director Wu's Speech: Director Wu then convened a meeting with all 140 staff members in the bureau's auditorium. He stated, "This is the first time I, Xingya, have met with everyone. I would like to discuss two points with you: (1) The Social Affairs Bureau, especially under the current circumstances, bears a very important responsibility and is closely related to various organizations and institutions. In the future, we must continue to follow the plans of the previous director and prioritize the urgent needs of society. For example, issues such as disaster relief in the war zone have comprehensive plans and instructions from the central government and the municipal government. The Social Affairs Bureau must diligently take on its responsibilities. Fortunately, all of you have a detailed understanding of the city's situation. In the future, if you have any suggestions that you believe are required by society and the public, you can propose concrete measures and consider implementing them. (2) In the past, general administrative personnel in any organization were uneasy during the transition between old and new leadership. This is the biggest flaw in Chinese politics. Staff members themselves often lose their jobs due to a lack of security, and the efficiency of the organization suffers due to frequent changes. When I served in Hubei and Anhui provinces, I did not advocate for changes to the staff. You can all continue to perform your duties as usual. I will act with impartiality and will not easily change those who work hard. This is what I hope everyone will pay special attention to." It is heard that Director Wu will hold a formal swearing-in ceremony on June 1st.

Beijing-Shanghai Railway

Night Trains to Resume from June 1st 114

Through Train Service from Xinlonghua to North Station Resumes Yesterday

After the Japanese military withdrew from the North Station on the afternoon of the 23rd, the Beijing-Shanghai Railway authorities resumed the Beijing-Shanghai through train service on the 24th. A reporter from the Huadong News Agency interviewed Mr. Zheng Baozhao, the Chief of the Traffic Department of the railway, yesterday regarding the recent arrangements. According to Mr. Zheng, since taking over the North Station on the 23rd of this month, the facilities along the line from the station to Qingyang Port have been completely destroyed. Under the guidance of Director Chen, various departments have worked hard to repair the train service within 24 hours. However, there have been many difficulties. For example, most of the locomotives in the Locomotive Department could not be repaired and restored to their original condition because the Wusong Locomotive Factory was occupied by the enemy and the Nanjing and Changzhou factories were small in scale and lacked facilities. Moreover, although the railway bureau had made considerable preparations for rolling stock and equipment since the end of February, Shanghai lacked these materials, so the facilities were still inadequate. We hope passengers will understand. The railway will try to restore the original condition as soon as possible to facilitate passengers. As for the traffic conditions, most of the telegraphs, telephones, electrical signals, railway signs, and signal flags between the stations from North Shanghai to Qingyang Port were damaged. The Electrical Engineering Department was unable to restore them temporarily due to a lack of telegraph lines, telephone copper wires, and electrical machinery. All trains arriving at the station will be guided by station staff to avoid danger. Therefore, the first day of resuming train service was extremely difficult, but in order to facilitate public transportation, we are still trying our best to manage it. Starting from the 26th, we have added one round trip each of the Beijing-Shanghai through train. At the same time, the railway line from Xinlonghua on the Shanghai-Hangzhou line to the North Station has also been repaired and through train service has resumed today (yesterday, the 27th), directly reaching the North Station as before. In addition, the reorganization of Beijing-Shanghai passenger trains is actively underway, but the most difficult problem is the shortage of locomotives and the damage to the facilities on passenger cars. We have asked the Locomotive Department to try to restore the original condition of the locomotives as soon as possible and to rush to install electric lights and other equipment on the cars. In short, for the convenience of the public, we have agreed with Director Chen that, no matter what, starting from June 1st, we must resume the Beijing-Shanghai night train service, that is, including the overnight trains, with four or five round trips of the Beijing-Shanghai through train and three or four round trips of the local trains each day, and try to restore freight trains. During this difficult planning period, we hope for the understanding and assistance of all sectors to restore the original condition as soon as possible.

Beijing and Fujian Authorities

Reply to Telegrams from Fujianese Organizations in Shanghai 121

After the representatives of the United Association of Fujianese Organizations in Shanghai visited Wang Jingwei and Chiang Kai-shek in Beijing, the military aspects were arranged, and the 19th Route Army was ordered to enter Fujian as soon as possible. The association has received letters from Wang Jingwei and telegrams from Fang Shengtao and Zhang Zhen in recent days, which are detailed below:

Wang Jingwei's letter (title omitted): "I met with you yesterday and received your letter. I am aware of everything. The fall of Zhangzhou has shocked all of Fujian. My colleagues in the government are deeply concerned. We have discussed the situation in detail with the Military Affairs Commission for several days and have reached a general decision, which will be announced soon. I hope you will understand. However, suppressing the communists should not rely solely on military force, but also on political reform. Military force is a temporary solution, while politics is the fundamental solution. Both should be emphasized. I hope that people's organizations can cooperate sincerely with the government to curb the rise of unrest and achieve governance. This is my heartfelt wish. Signed, Wang Jingwei."

Fang Shengtao's telegram (title omitted): "I have received your telegram. The communist scourge in our homeland must be eliminated as soon as possible. We are actively planning and, as soon as the arrangements are in place, I will personally lead the provincial departments to eliminate them. I am ashamed that inadequate precautions have caused you to be concerned from afar. Thank you for your encouragement. I will work hard to live up to your expectations. I hope that you, who care for our homeland, will provide guidance at any time so that I may improve. Signed, Fang Shengtao."

Zhang Zhen's reply telegram (title omitted): "I have received your telegram. The communist scourge concerns the whole country and is not a local issue. The plan to suppress the communists requires overall planning and cannot be accomplished by a small number of troops. The main forces of the communists entering Fujian are the First and Fifth Army Corps. The forces attacking Zhangzhou were the elite of these army corps. The Third, Fourth, Fourteenth, and Fifteenth Armies, and several independent divisions, totaling about 30,000 men, were after the battle of Shiyong in Longyan, we could only gather our forces, defend the key passes, and fight hard for more than ten days. The enemy and our forces suffered about 4,000 casualties each. Exhausted and without reinforcements, I painfully took responsibility for abandoning the city. The situation in Fujian is complex, and Zhang has spread rumors, saying that we retreated without a fight. The facts are there and need no explanation. I have been stationed in Zhangzhou for four years and have always strived to build up the region in various ways. I am committed to our homeland and, as a soldier, I would not abandon Zhangzhou unless absolutely necessary. This heart of mine will be understood by those who know the situation. We are reorganizing our forces and striving to counterattack. The vanguard has advanced to Zhangpu, Shijiao Dong, Punan, and other places. If we can get help from friendly forces, we will be able to recover Zhangzhou in the near future. The newspapers in the country are a reflection of evil intentions. After the communists invaded Zhangzhou, provincial news even reported that Sun Lianzhong or the Guangdong army were passing through to resist the Japanese. The disruption and absurdity are truly heartbreaking. You, who love your homeland and country, must be aware of the facts and not be blinded by rumors. As long as I have breath, my will will not falter and I will not abandon my responsibility. We must fight to the end together. Signed, Zhang Zhen Ma."

Taicang Native Place Association

Opposes the Chief County Being Moved to Jiading 125

The Jiangsu Provincial Government recently announced that it would divide the province into fifteen administrative regions, with each region having a chief county to supervise the administration of the entire region. The method of division is to establish the chief county in the former government or prefecture seat. However, Taicang was originally a directly subordinate state, but the chief county that should have been established was changed to Jiading. The Taicang Native Place Association in Shanghai believes that the facilities are different and expresses its opposition. It called a meeting yesterday and decided to send a telegram to the provincial government requesting that the former practice be followed. The text of the telegram is as follows: "To Chairman Gu of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, it is reported that all former government and prefecture seats will be chief counties, but Taicang, which should have a chief county, has been changed to Jiading, which is different. Please continue to designate Taicang as the chief county, called the Taicang Region, to show uniformity and avoid disputes. Signed, Taicang Native Place Association in Shanghai."

Municipal Police Bureau Conducts Household Registration Check

Notice Limited to Reporting by the End of This Month 129

Residents in the Chinese areas of this city, due to the Sino-Japanese war, have moved away one after another, resulting in changes in household registration. Most of these changes have not been registered. Now, the Municipal Public Bureau considers that order is gradually returning to normal, and residents moving in and out, births, deaths, and inheritances should all be registered in accordance with the regulations, so as to emphasize the important administration of household registration. Therefore, a notice has been issued, limiting all residents to report to the police station in charge by the end of this month. While some residents have complied with the report, there are also many who have delayed in reporting. Therefore, in recent days, all police districts have sent household registration police officers to conduct detailed investigations in each household within their jurisdiction, and have also informed all residents that if there are any changes in the future, they should report them at any time.

Yu Yan, Director of the Business Department of the Ministry of Railways, Organizes Opinions on Railways

Telegrams to All Routes Soliciting Rescue and Improvement Plans

Yu Yan, Director of the Business Department of the Ministry of Railways, recently published his thoughts on reorganizing railway business and improving railway administration, stating that in the past ten years, the railway administration has been passively perfunctory, and has become increasingly degraded and corrupt, causing the railways across the country to become almost a kind of duty-bound agency. The various routes have gradually become rotten and can no longer be renovated and reorganized. Therefore, starting from the personnel aspect to reorganize, the spirit of fairness, integrity, and struggle should be the method of improvement. Abiding by the law, being open and impartial is called fairness, being legal, reasonable, and in line with national and people's well-being is called righteousness, not being perfunctory is called integrity, being clean and devoted to public service is called cleanliness, invigorating the spirit is called struggle, and striving tirelessly is called fighting. Although these three points contain many meanings, they are the only way to defeat the bureaucratization of the administration of various routes. To improve railway business, one should engage in commercialization, (A) increasing transportation efficiency, (1) recovering all military vehicles, (2) reducing the number of delayed tons of various routes and increasing the number of delayed ton miles, (3) improving the freight yards and improving the roads of various routes, (4) improving the management methods of the porters and transshipment companies of various routes, (B) promoting responsible transportation. Since the Siping-Taonan Railway began to implement it in the ninth year of the Republic of China, its business income has increased dramatically year by year, from more than one million to six million. Last year, the Beining Railway only operated eleven stations. During the year, except for three months when the route was divided by the violent Japanese, there were only nine months. Statistics show that the total turnover has increased to 40 million. From the perspective of responsible transportation alone, it has also increased by more than 3,297,000 yuan. This achievement can be used as an example. (C) Implementing commercial management methods, (1) improving the equipment of each station, (2) paying attention to scientific management methods, (3) promoting business solicitation, (4) making all rules and regulations public, (5) conducting detailed investigations of the industrial and commercial enterprises along the routes of various routes and finding ways to connect, (6) promoting domestic routes and water and land combined transportation methods. All of these are temporary solutions to the current business. As for the fundamental reorganization plan, how to reorganize the debts of various routes to restore railway credit, how to plan the engineering equipment of various routes, and increase the number of locomotives, all require huge amounts of money. This is the entire railway reorganization plan, which will be carried out at any time after discussing with the Deputy Minister of the Ministry and the various departments, in order to gradually improve. Also, Yu sent a telegram to the colleagues of the various routes, saying, "To the public of the colleagues of the various routes, I am taking the position of department director with my mediocre and shallow abilities. I have insufficient knowledge and weak ambition. I hope to add the views of loyalty and benefit, and I am not afraid to tell each other ten times. I hope to use the mistakes of other mountains to attack jade, and do not hesitate to leave a thousand thoughts behind. If there is anything that is not done, I am willing to hear good words. If you come to teach, I will wait sincerely." Yu Yan, Director of the Business Department of the Ministry of Railways, has a seal.

Yao Benyuan Transferred to the Director of the Second Station in the Seventh District 134

Yao Benyuan, the director of the Second Station in the Third District of Shanghai, has served as the director of various district offices of the Public Security Bureau. The residents love him, and his political reputation is very good. His integrity is especially praised. After the resumption of business, the market was depressed, and the business also fell sharply, and the economic hardship was very different from the past. It is ridiculous to say that they have tripled their profits. A Young Girl's Quarrel Causes a Death 148

Jiang Shoubao Commits Suicide by Swallowing Opium

Jiang Shoubao, a 13-year-old Wuxi girl living at No. 629 East Tangjia Lane, had a quarrel with a neighbor girl, Qian Amao, 14 years old, at about 7 pm on the 25th of this month. After the quarrel, she secretly swallowed opium and committed suicide that night. After her mother noticed, she immediately reported it to the relevant Huishi Police Station and ordered detectives to investigate. The girl was sent to Guangren Hospital for treatment, but she died of poisoning the next day. The body was taken to the Xiyanshi Institute on Feilun Road. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Local Court was requested to appoint Prosecutor Guo Wei, along with forensic doctor Wei Ligong and secretary Wang Zuyi, to go to the institute to investigate the body. Ascending the seat of office, according to Qian Amao's confession, "I was selling newspapers in the lane that day, and Jiang was scolding me behind my back. Later, I also scolded him back a few times, and there was no other accident." According to Jiang Li's complaint, "The deceased is my daughter, and her husband died early. At about 6 pm the night before, I went to Tongfu Road for something. Unexpectedly, when I returned home, I saw that the girl's face was very different, and she told me that she had swallowed opium." The reason was because she had a quarrel with Qian Amao, and Qian's parents beat my daughter and burned her neck with cigarette butts. Neighbors and my brother all witnessed it at that time. If she had not been beaten, she would not have committed suicide." Mr. Guo declared that the deceased was indeed poisoned to death by swallowing opium before her death. The body was handed over to the mother of the corpse, who signed a guarantee to take it back for burial.

Wang Yuanlong Sues Zhang Shichuan 149

Both Parties Found Not Guilty

The famous director Wang Yuanlong, who is currently the leading actor in the Longma Film Company, signed a contract with Zhang Shichuan, the manager of the Star Film Company, in August last year to shoot the film "Water Margin". Later, because the film was banned by the authorities, Zhang sued Wang in the First Special District Court for civil reasons for owing money. At that time, the newspapers also published this matter. However, after Wang Yuanlong was sued, he believed that Zhang's publicity in the newspapers had completely destroyed his reputation, causing him great losses for almost a year. Therefore, he also hired lawyer Ge Cheng to sue Zhang Shichuan in the Special Court for defamation. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Fu Lin opened a court to hear the case. The defendant Zhang Shichuan did not arrive, and lawyer Zhan Jifeng was appointed to appear in court as his agent. He also filed a counterclaim for false accusation, that is, according to the complaint of the plaintiff Wang Yuanlong, the above situation was true and that he did not owe Zhang's money. Therefore, the lawsuit was also won at that time, but Zhang's publicity in the newspapers damaged my reputation, causing me great losses. I should ask to investigate. Then lawyer Zhan Jifeng said that this case was actually caused by the plaintiff making waves out of nothing, filing a lawsuit, and wanting the defendant to be punished criminally. He also stated the circumstances of the civil litigation and submitted the previous judgments for filing, and filed a counterclaim, falsely accusing him of requesting to be punished according to the law. At the end of the debate by the lawyers of both parties, Judge Fu ruled in court that Wang Yuanlong and Zhang Shichuan were both not guilty. Wang Yuanlong's ancillary civil litigation was transferred to the civil court for trial.

Youthful Carjacking Case 150

The Car Returned Intact

The Purpose of the Theft Remains Unknown

Yesterday afternoon at 5:25 PM, a hurried customer, appearing to be a local youth, about thirty years old, wearing a gray jacket and a felt hat, entered the Asia Automobile Company at 107 Avenue Dubail in the French Concession. Claiming to be named Wang, he asked the company accountant the hourly rental rate. The accountant replied that the minimum price was three silver dollars per hour. The hurried customer immediately paid three dollars, saying he needed to go to Longhua. The chauffeur, Zhao Alin from Yangzhou, was assigned a Shunfeng sedan with a French Concession license plate number 12192 (Shanghai City 41040). When the car reached the entrance of Lane Sande on Avenue Saepe, the youth suddenly ordered the car to stop and called out to a person standing at the lane entrance wearing a black raincoat. The two then sat side by side, and the car drove south. After reaching Xujiahui Road and crossing the Jinguiji Bridge, it arrived at Xietu Road. At that time, the youth ordered the car to drive west. When it reached about a hundred paces west of Mingde School, the youth again ordered the car to stop. The two jumped out of the car together, forced the chauffeur out of the car, and forbade him from making any noise, saying they needed to borrow the car for a while and would return it shortly. The youth then got back into the car and drove off at lightning speed. The person in the raincoat watched over the chauffeur. About half an hour later, the person in the raincoat told the chauffeur in a low voice that the car was parked on Zhongshan Road and that he could go and get it. After saying this, he left. The chauffeur then walked west to Zhongshan Road, but could not find the car anywhere. He then went to the Longhua Headquarters and the Public Security Bureau to report the incident. At that time, a chauffeur from the Headquarters who was passing by Jinguiji Bridge on official business saw the car that had been stolen and told Zhao Alin. When Zhao rushed to Jinguiji Road, he indeed saw the car parked by the roadside. Everything in the car was intact. He immediately drove the car back, which was already after 8:00 PM. However, the true purpose of the hurried customer stealing the car remains unknown.

Gu Zilin and Others Almost Trapped

Zhang Bin Flees with Funds, Disappearing Without a Trace

Zhang Bin, also known as Zhang Yulin and Zhang Zhenting, from Xuzhou, residing at 285 Yuqing Lane, Avenue Messimy in the French Concession, along with accomplices Song Ziping (from Anhui) and Peng Yifu (also known as Peng Jifu, from Jiangxi), claimed to have recruited thousands of volunteer soldiers in Henan and needed funds for their deployment. Education News

Important News

Ministry of Education Orders That No Entrance Examination May Be Cancelled Without Permission 164

Nanjing, 28th. The Ministry of Education has formulated provisional regulations for graduation entrance examinations for primary and secondary school students and has issued a circular to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities. If any province, city, or district has special circumstances that prevent it from holding a secondary school entrance examination, it must first submit a report to the Ministry for approval and record. If any county or city primary school cannot hold an entrance examination, the local educational administrative organs should describe the local situation and submit it to the responsible Education Department for review and record.

Ministry of Education Issues Circular Ordering Universities to Extend Enrollment Deadlines as Appropriate 165

Nanjing, 28th. According to a report from the Jiangxi Education Department, universities hold entrance examinations for new students in early July each year, while middle schools in various provinces often hastily end the courses and hold graduation examinations in advance in order to accommodate students applying for further education. However, even with this, the time is too short and transportation is difficult, and many students traveling from afar often arrive late. Therefore, they requested that all universities and educational institutions in the country be notified to postpone the entrance examination periods appropriately starting from the next academic year. The Ministry has now issued a circular to all schools to consider and implement this.

Some Changes to the Jiangsu Provincial Experimental Primary School 166

Normal Schools Independently Implement Attached Primary Schools to Become Experimental Primary Schools with Exclusive Responsibility for Experimentation

The Jiangsu Education Department has decided to implement an independent system for normal schools and has designated Zhenjiang Middle School and eight other schools to specialize in normal school education in the future. Starting next year, they will no longer enroll general education students. The experimental primary schools originally attached to these schools will naturally be changed to attached primary schools for normal school students to practice and research effective teaching methods for local primary schools to emulate. The experimental primary schools attached to middle schools that have not been changed to normal schools will still be called experimental primary schools, with the exclusive responsibility for experimenting with new teaching methods, and will gradually enrich their content in order to complete the above mission. However, before all the normal school students originally in the middle schools have graduated, the names of the primary schools may be changed, but the original tasks will not be changed much. This matter has been communicated to the middle schools and experimental primary schools for information. The Education Department's instructions are extracted below:

In order to emphasize normal school education, cultivate excellent teachers, and achieve the goal of universal compulsory education, this Department has decided to adopt an independent system for normal schools. Starting in 1932, Zhenjiang, Wuxi, Taicang, Rugao, Huaiyin, and Donghai Middle Schools, as well as Suzhou and Xuzhou Girls' Middle Schools, will be designated to establish normal school departments and will not enroll general education students. All other provincial middle schools will no longer enroll normal school students. It has been communicated to all schools to comply. The experimental primary schools currently in the provincial middle schools are mostly reorganized from the primary schools attached to the former normal schools. At that time, the organizational changes were made because of the emphasis on experimental work. However, because the experimental work was just starting and the plans were complicated, the original task of normal school students' practice was sometimes not fully considered, resulting in the feeling that the most recent graduating normal school students lacked teaching experience. Now that the independent normal schools have been restored, the organization of the attached primary schools should be changed accordingly to suit the actual situation.

It is now decided that starting in 1932, the experimental primary schools attached to the middle schools designated to specialize in normal school education, including Zhenjiang Middle School Experimental Primary School, Wuxi Middle School Experimental Primary School, Taicang Middle School Experimental Primary School, Huaiyin Middle School Experimental Primary School, Donghai Middle School Experimental Primary School, Suzhou Girls' Middle School Experimental Primary School, and Xuzhou Girls' Middle School Experimental Primary School, should all uniformly cancel the experimental designation. Together with the primary school department of Rugao Middle School, they will all be renamed "Attached Primary School of [Middle School Name]," with special emphasis on the teaching practice of normal school students. They will also research and improve effective teaching methods for local primary schools to emulate. The remaining South Middle School Experimental Primary School, South Girls' Middle School Experimental Primary School, Suzhou Middle School Experimental Primary School, Tongzhou Middle School Experimental Primary School, Xuzhou Middle School Experimental Primary School, Yangzhou Middle School Experimental Primary School, and Songjiang Girls' Middle School Experimental Primary School will still use the old experimental name and will be solely responsible for experimenting with temporary education methods. The results of the research will be shared with the attached primary schools to jointly improve local primary schools and gradually enrich their content in order to complete the above mission. Before all the normal school students in these middle schools have graduated, the original teaching practice should still be carried out as before, and guidance should be strengthened. The organizational regulations for attached primary schools will be drafted and promulgated separately, and the organizational regulations for experimental primary schools should be amended and promulgated separately. This order is hereby issued to the principals of the schools for their information. This order.

Pudong Middle School Closed This Semester 170

News from the Pudong Middle School Board of Directors: Pudong Middle School has been closed for one semester since the January 28th Shanghai Incident due to the dangerous location, obstructed transportation, and the fact that most of the students are from Guangdong and Sichuan, who have all returned home to transfer to nearby schools or study at other schools. The school board of directors immediately resolved to close the school for one semester. The principal formally notified the students' parents and reported it to the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau for record. Now that Shanghai has been restored, the school board of directors is properly planning a thorough reorganization and preparing to open the school early next semester and provide all kinds of assistance to students' studies. The news reported yesterday that the teachers and students of the school jointly formed a school affairs maintenance committee and that the school would open on June 1st is completely rumored and not factual.

Ancient Temple Bell Records (8) Not · Remove · Courtyard · Grass · Cottage · Husband · 172

Ten

"Mr. Zhang! Please sit in my temple room for a while. I'll talk to you when I've finished ringing the bell."

With that, I went to ring my dawn bell. As I walked, I thought, this bearded man has given me a difficult problem. I must refuse him. But he has some influence in the countryside. He is more than capable of ruining something but is not enough to fix it, I must be careful. Although I must refuse him, I must not offend him. It's never a good thing for enemies to meet. The fact that I’m waking him up from his opium den with the bell is already more than enough to bear. Now I'm promoting the establishment of a school, and he wants to be a teacher. It's so coincidental that it's truly laughable and annoying. But what to do? ... I rang the bell and walked into the room, only to find Zhang the Bearded Man lying on my bed snoring. Is this the effect of the dawn bell? Does he have to fall asleep when he hears my dawn bell? Who knows? Okay, let him sleep, I'll wake him up when I have a solution.

I have it! This school should be run by all the people in the village. Who can act alone? Who can privately pass it down? Good, let's do that. Each family will send a representative to the temple to discuss it together. The more I think about it, the more I feel this is the fairest method. I can't think of anything better. So I walked through the village, greeting each family and saying, "Please send one representative from each family to the temple to discuss opening a school and hiring a teacher. Come when you hear my bell ring." ... The children happily said, "A school is opening ... we'll have a school to go to ..."

After greeting everyone, I returned to the temple to arrange everything. How will these people hold a meeting? Since the creation of the world, this village has never held a formal meeting. I have no such experience either. This founding meeting is so important, can we just hold it casually? That's right, I have a book on meeting rules in my drawer. Why don't I take it out and take a look? This book was given to me by a young tourist. Now this book has become our only guide. I thought that I could flip through it a few times, get a general idea, and then start ringing the bell. In reality, it wasn't that easy. I was too hasty in this matter, like digging a well when I was thirsty. But I thought that digging a well when I was thirsty was still trying to find a solution through my own efforts, which was better than standing there waiting for it to rain. I spent more than two hours reading to figure out the important secrets of holding a meeting. Then I boldly went to ring the bell to convene the founding meeting.

The school's work is being carried out with professors and students jointly forming a school affairs design committee. This spirit of cooperation is proposing fundamental plans to seek the development of school affairs. The school's new charter will soon be printed, and the improvements in organization and education will be determined in the new charter.

In the past ten days, students at the school have been striving to demonstrate a spirit of unity, and various societies have been fully established. There are four organizations: the Political Science Society, the Educational Society, the Science Society, and the Commerce Society. The Political Science Society has initiated a joint effort by all the societies to conduct research and investigation on various aspects after the Songhu Anti-Japanese War. It is planned to compile the results of the research and investigation into a series of books or special publications for contribution.

Market Overview Yesterday, in the Japanese street silver and money industry, there were many transactions in the morning and afternoon markets due to the majority of securities being sold for delivery. However, the morning market still had bank purchases to support it, and the silver dollar price did not change much. The afternoon market saw stagnation in purchases and a strong selling atmosphere, making it difficult for prices to hold steady. As the trend became increasingly weak, it was always difficult to expect a firm price. Since the silver base was in the middle of the general closing period, there was no hope of rising either. Silver demolition price. The supply and demand for foreign silver dollars in the morning market were equal, so although competition was fierce, the price did not rise or fall, remaining the same as the previous afternoon, at 7 qian zero zero one hao two hu and a half. The selling atmosphere suddenly flourished in the afternoon market, and the price fell by half a li, calculated as six qian nine fen nine li six hao two hu and a half. As a result, it fell by two hao and a half compared to the morning market the day before. The silver demolition price in the morning and afternoon markets both opened at 7 fen, one fen higher than the previous day. Important News on Domestic New Cotton Production 200

Recently, letters have been received from cotton-producing provinces and regions, covering the overall situation of cotton production. Due to last year's flood, farmers have no power to cultivate the land, and this year's production will inevitably be reduced. It has been raining for more than half a month in Hubei Province, and cotton production has been even more damaged.

Shanxi (Letter of the 15th): The situation of cotton production this year is still unlikely to be a bumper harvest. Due to the lack of rain this spring, each county did not receive three or four inches of rain until the 5th of this month. However, the sowing period seems to be slightly late.

Silk and Tea

Wuxi Spring Silkworm Season Early or Late County

Early Silkworm Cocoons Seen New, Late Silkworms Only Three Sleeps 201

The spring silkworms in the four villages of Wuxi have a difference of about two weeks between the early and late silkworm seasons. The early silkworms have suffered damage due to the weather, and 60% to 70% have been abandoned. Early silkworm cocoons have been seen new. However, after the silkworms were on the racks, due to thunderstorms and extreme cold, the silkworm ants did not spin enough silk, and the silkworms were thin and inferior. Very few cocoons were opened for weighing. This kind of inferior cocoon was refused and not accepted. Slightly superior cocoons originally opened at only 15 or 16 yuan, but now it is only 20 yuan. The late silkworms, which are being raised by the silkworm households, only have three sleeps. The climate is unevenly warm and cold, and the development is not smooth. However, it is slightly better than the early silkworm flood. The price of leaves is currently sold at 1 yuan and 45 corners.

Foreign Silk Firms in Dire Straits 202

Yesterday, the Shanghai foreign silk market remained stagnant and lifeless. It was found that New York raw silk prices continued to decline, and factory managers and others also became weary. Various silk mills are focusing on rayon and Japanese silk as raw materials, causing the market to weaken to an extreme. No one inquired about Chinese silk. Both spot and futures silk in Shanghai remained suspended, indicating the silk market has fallen into dire straits.

High Prices and Flourishing Trade for New Tea in Wuyuan 203

New tea from Wuyuan has been opening for sale in large quantities since the day before yesterday. Tea farmers have sold almost a third of their tea reserves. Today (the 20th), Dragon Isle tea, known for its superior quality among northern Wuyuan tea leaves, was opened for sale by Cantonese merchants, priced at 80 yuan. Qinghua Zhangcun tea was priced at 70 yuan, Xikeng tea at 74 yuan, Nanxiang Kaoshui tea at 48 yuan, and Yaocun Duan tea at 51 yuan. The market momentum continues to rise. However, high-grade tea from various villages above Dayuan and Fengshan in the eighth district is not yet being traded in large quantities, as harvesting and processing are not fully completed. Various shops in Sikou and Zhangcun are rushing to produce “core-extracted” tea and have scheduled sorting to begin tomorrow. According to recent investigations, more than ten new shops have been added in Wubei Yanchuan, Wangcun, Gao'an, and Dragon, among other places. Among them, Gao'an Qian Jixiang is a Shanghai Cantonese shop that relocated to Wuyuan this year due to the destruction of its warehouse in Zhabei.

Qimen Black Tea Third Batch Approaching Completion 204

The various batches of Qimen black tea, except for the first and second batches that have been successively shipped to Shanghai, the third batch will soon be fully stacked within days. By the end of this month, all batches are expected to be completed. According to statistics from Qimen tea merchants, the amount of tea purchased by various shops this year is 30-40% less than in previous years, with each shop buying no more than 300 boxes. This is because there was a lot of rain during the picking season, resulting in weak production. Later, when the weather cleared, the tea leaves were already old and the plants were no longer tender. The final mountain price also fell to 30 yuan. Economically sound shops are still processing floral-scented tea. Currently, various shops are hoping that the first and second batches will be sold profitably, and they will need to continue processing subsidiary batches when new tea emerges.

Qimen Tea Trade Still Thriving 205

Yesterday, the foreign tea market saw active trading in Qimen, Fuliang, and other types of black tea. Over 3,300 boxes were traded throughout the market. Top prices remained at 200 taels, and the situation has become more stable than before. However, the green tea market remains sluggish. There were no transactions for high-grade Zhenmei tea. Foreign firms such as Jardine Matheson, Wing On, and Tong Fu have purchased over 600 boxes of native Zhenmei and Zhenmei needles, but prices are consistently declining. About twenty boxes of Gongxi tea from Donglu, Wuyuan, arrived yesterday. It is reported that white-label merchants are offering prices that are 10-20 taels lower than before. Chinese tea merchants are unwilling to sell due to high costs, and no new prices have been established yet.

Dexing Tea Difficult to Sell Due to Banditry 206

This year's Dexing new tea is of tender and high-quality. Due to financial constraints, mountain farmers, even though their residences have been occupied by bandits, are seizing the opportunity to return home to harvest and process new tea. Because they cannot store the tea at home, they are willing to sell it cheaply. Top and middle-grade tea is only selling for 20 to 19 yuan per dan (unit of weight). Common tea merchants, enticed by the prospect of high profits, are braving danger to travel to the seventh, eighth, and ninth districts to purchase tea. Tea purchased in Dexing can be sold for 50 to 60 yuan per dan in Wuyuan, resulting in a profit of 30 to 40 yuan per dan. Recently, tea merchants from Sikou and Changtan in Wuyuan went to the Xinjian area to purchase tea but were discovered by communist bandits. One tea merchant from Sikou was captured, and the rest abandoned their tea and fled. As a result, merchants who were going to Dexing to purchase tea are all deterred and dare not consider it anymore.
