Free Talk

Sword Grinding Record

Ran Zhen'ao 212

— Gu Mingdao

You have already described the events involving the old man at the noodle shop. Now, I will tell you about Ran Zhen and He Yahu's killing of enemies, which is truly spirited. Let me first record Ran Zhen's story. After the Japanese army invaded our Liaoning and Jilin provinces, the ruling authorities raised the banner of non-resistance. The day of returning our rivers and mountains was nowhere in sight. However, the people of the Eastern Provinces suffered greatly under the Japanese army's poison, their homes turned to ruins, and the fields filled with white bones. Most of them had become people without a country or home. Therefore, volunteer armies rose up in various places, engaging in field battles with the Japanese army, shedding blood and throwing their heads, repeatedly defeating strong enemies. To this day, their momentum is quite strong, and the Japanese army has been unable to suppress them. Ran Zhen was from Niuzhuang and made a living driving a donkey cart. He had served in the military and was capable of fighting with a gun. Later, he deserted after offending his superiors. He was known for his chivalry in the neighborhoods, and was quite famous among the common people. The great bandit Lao Beifeng hated the brutality of the Japanese and rose up in rebellion, leading his followers in a night attack on Niuzhuang. The defending Japanese army responded hastily, and the volunteer army fought bravely, defeating the Japanese army. Ran Zhen arose in the night, wearing his clothes and gripping a wooden stick. He rushed to the Japanese army camp and hid in a dark corner. When a Japanese soldier retreated, he leaped forward and struck the soldier with his stick, causing him to fall to the ground. He then seized the soldier's gun and bullets and joined the volunteer army to fight, killing many Japanese soldiers. He also led the volunteer army in a fierce pursuit. This battle greatly frightened the Japanese army, and Lao Beifeng admired his courage and greatly appreciated him. Later, the Japanese army reinforced and counterattacked, and the volunteer army was forced to retreat due to strategic considerations. Ran Zhen also went with them. I do not know if this loyal and brave anti-Japanese warrior is still in the army today.

The Shanghai Broadsword Teams 213

— Shi Yan Ye

During the month-long bloody battle against the Japanese in Shanghai, the broadsword teams participated in the killing of enemies with unparalleled loyalty and courage. This is universally acknowledged. Here, I will describe the types of broadsword teams to fill in the gaps in this publication.

The broadsword team that uses only broadswords has no other weapons. During battle, they are positioned behind the infantry and cavalry. When close combat ensues, they leap to the front lines with a shout. Wherever their broadswords strike, they are invincible. Whenever the Japanese see the glint of the blade, their knees involuntarily bend or their feet turn backward. These men are either selected and trained from the soldiers or come from the general public, stirred by righteous indignation. They are all men of passion.

The broadsword team that also uses broadswords is essentially the infantry in the army. These men carry long guns and broadswords on their backs. During battle, they use their guns for long-range attacks. For close combat, they use the gun with the bayonet, but the bayonet is not as quick or effective as the broadsword. When Liu Zhi's First Division was stationed in Wuchang last month, I saw that the infantry in his army each carried a broadsword on their back.

The broadsword team with full weapons, in addition to the broadsword, also carries a Mauser pistol on their waist and hand grenades. Daggers are hidden in cloth bindings on both legs. During battle, if the situation is suitable for using a gun, the Mauser pistol fires like a string of pearls. If hand grenades are needed, they are thrown accurately. If the enemy's bullets come like rain and there is no way to avoid them, they wield their broadswords, and a cold light flashes. You cannot see the person, but you hear the bullets being deflected by the blade, making a clanging sound. The bullets cannot reach their bodies. Those skilled in using swords in Chinese martial arts wear white clothes. When they dance passionately, you only see the glint of swords and the chilling aura. If splashed with thick ink, it would all become a barrier of blades. When they finish dancing, their white clothes would not have a single stain. Perhaps the broadsword teams also possess this divine skill. They engage in bloody combat with the enemy, using their broadswords to chop and slash. Those who are struck are killed instantly. If their precious sword is unfortunately broken, they discard it and draw their daggers. They dance wildly with their short knives, and are also invincible. This broadsword team with full weapons is effective in long-range attacks and close combat. They are always victorious.

The Scenery of the Temple Fair 214

— Parrot

Miscellaneous Writings of the Old Capital (6)

The temple fair is almost a remnant of the ancient market system.

Every month on certain days, Funei Avenue is flooded with crowds of people, and many vendors add their stalls to the roadside. You can also hear the clamor of gongs and drums from the street performers, the solo performance of the Hu Jia by the street artists, the clear battles of the opium smokers, and many other hawking sounds. This continues for three days, and everyone knows that there is a temple fair at the White Pagoda Temple.

In Beijing, the temple fair is not limited to the White Pagoda Temple. I also know of one at Huguo Temple in the city and one at the hot springs outside the city. However, because I live near the White Pagoda Temple, I am more familiar with the situation there. In fact, all temple fairs are similar.

When the day of the temple fair arrives, the people nearby excitedly rush to attend, and there are also those who hire rickshaws from afar to visit. Especially the children nearby, on the day of the temple fair, they all smile and excitedly rush into the temple fair, because at that time they can see the big girls bathing in the peep show, watch the monkey show performed by Shandong people, listen to temporary Bangzi operas for three copper coins, and drink Dutch water for one copper coin per cup. In short, they believe that everything in the temple fair can attract their young minds and make them forget to return home. In the temple fair, in addition to things to watch, almost all daily necessities are sold. There are materials for making short shirts for young boys, fancy stationery for female students to write love letters, and jewelry for decorating women. However, the prices are cheaper than on the streets outside. Although this is the reason why ladies and young women who like to buy expensive foreign goods do not frequent the temple fair, the people below the middle class flock to it. Naturally, there are market prices here that suit their tastes, and the temple fair is almost reserved for these people below the middle class.

I spent ten copper coins in the temple fair to buy a pot of Zinnia, and I happily carried it back to my residence, because I wanted it to flourish day by day, so I served it every day like serving an old master, catching bugs and watering it a lot. However, in less than a week, the flowers drooped and the leaves withered. So, I looked forward to the next temple fair, so I could buy another pot.

In Memory of the Martyrs Who Died in the Anti-Japanese War in Shanghai 215

— Xu Shiying Dong

Looking at Ryukyu and Korea, south to Taiwan and Penghu, north to Lushun and Dalian. Iron blood strengthens the golden pot, and we will avenge our country for nine generations.

First battle Yanze, second battle Nomura, third battle Ueda. Green mountains bury white bones, and thousands of families cry tears for loyal souls.

Huang Yanpei 216

The bugle horns startle and turn back the Shanghai tide, and a small army is proud of the insects and sand. Knowing that you were careless and lost the hard-to-attack city, you must regret sending your troops to raid from afar. Your great ambition was rewarded like Qin Bolang, and your prestige ultimately belonged to Han Piaoyao. Men lightly value life and death when serving their country, singing and crying, sharing drinks and writing great appeals.

From the beginning, divine courage relied on sincerity, and we still hear the sound of killing thieves in the dark sky. Sages and heroes have all died for a hundred years, and half of the heroes have no name for eternity. Who will turn the world's peaceful situation around? It should be evaluated in the Spring and Autumn Annals as a righteous war. Keep the good model of unwavering loyalty, and may a good name be bestowed upon the newborn nineteen (just one month after "January 28th," a grandson was born and named Nineteen).

Chen Ruxuan 217

For thirty-five days, the spirit of resistance filled the mountains and seas, shaking the past and shining on the present. Thinking of the lone army advancing alone at that time, invincible in their path. The brave warriors had already given their lives to fulfill their vows. What is there to fear from ten thousand deaths? They only sought to win a few points of popular sentiment, sweeping away the island country that swallows the East Sea.

For hundreds of years, the history of diplomacy has been one of holding back resentment and shame, stepping forward and then backward. Sighing that to this day, hundreds of ills are rampant, and things are getting worse and worse. The esteemed gentlemen are ultimately engaging in empty talk of revolution, with no plan. It is unbearable to retreat three times from the Japanese invaders and celebrate peace under the city walls.

Tidbits 218

— Ping

"Sofu" and "Lafu" are both very peculiar terms in the East. "Sofu" originated in Japan, and "Lafu" is a product left over by our Chinese warlords. Yesterday, the newspaper reported that "Chen Jitang's troops were recruiting in the Guangsan Road area…" This is an ominous sign, and may be the beginning of another tragic scene of fratricide! During the twenty years of civil war, "Lafu" has left us with an incomprehensible sense of sorrow and trauma! The tighter the "Lafu" is pulled, the worse the situation becomes. Conversely, when fighting for the survival of the country and seeking the interests of the nation, such as the Northern Expedition fifteen years ago and the recent Battle of Shanghai, who would not be eager to participate in the war? How could there be a kidnapping-style "Lafu"? Therefore, the people fear "Lafu," which is to oppose civil war. Whoever forces "Lafu" is the demon of civil war!

The Tomb of Sima Yi 219

— Zhang Yan

Sima Yi was a hero. I once visited his tomb and now recall what I saw to share with the readers.

It is located outside the north gate of the current capital (Luoyang), about three miles from the city and two miles from the east railway station. The terrain along the way is undulating and the roads are rugged. The tomb faces south and has a majestic appearance. There are no stone figures of civil or military officials or stone beasts at the mausoleum gate, nor are there tall, arched tomb trees. The rampant grass and desolate smoke create an extremely desolate scene. There is a stone stele in front of the tomb, engraved with the six characters "Emperor Xuan of Jin, Highland Mausoleum." The tomb site covers an area of more than ten acres and is about ten zhang (unit of length) tall. There is a hole in the center of the top that gradually narrows and is so deep that it cannot be seen. The elders of Luoyang say that a certain villager hated his treachery and sold his good head to a foreign country for the price of 100,000 gold yuan. If this is true, I am afraid that the stubborn Zhongda must be stroking his severed neck underground, boasting that his unsightly gray-white face could fetch such a good price. About two or three hundred steps to the right of Sima's tomb, there is a stone stele of the Li family's ancestral tomb. One says that it is the ancestral tomb of Li Hongzhang of Hefei, because it is buried on the dragon vein, so Hongzhang was granted the title of Duke. This statement is far-fetched and should not be taken seriously. However, I have indeed seen the stone stele of the Li family's ancestral tomb. It is impossible to know if it is connected to Hongzhang.

Reading Zeng's Stele at Dafengtang (Part 1) 220

— Zizai

Zhang Daqian came from Weitang yesterday and invited me to Dafengtang to discuss art. Zhang Ershanzi, Xie Dayu, Cen Ludan, and other gentlemen were also present. We read art, tasted tea, and discussed the past and present. The room was filled with joy, and the host and guests were very happy. Then, Shanzi presented Chen Sanli's (Poetry Elder) newly composed inscription for the tomb of the famous calligrapher Zeng Nongran. The Zhang brothers were Zeng Nongran's students and excelled in painting and calligraphy. After Nongran's death, they joined with their fellow students to organize the Zeng-Li Alumni Association, holding memorial services in spring and autumn to commemorate their teacher's virtue. It is rare to see this in the end times. Nongran's remains had already been transported back to his hometown for burial, but the inscription was still missing. His eldest son traveled to Lushan to ask the Elder Sanli to write an inscription, elaborating on Nongran's literary achievements and virtues, and describing his intimacy with Qing Daoren and Sanli in detail. However, the friendship between the two is also fully revealed in the lines. Nongran in the afterlife must be smiling and stroking his beard. The inscription is recorded as follows.

Inscription for the Tomb of the Late Zeng, Official of the Ministry of War in the Qing Dynasty, written by Chen Sanli of Yining. The deceased was named Zeng Xi, courtesy name Ziji, formerly Siyuan, and later known as Nongran. His family has been from Hengyang for generations. He was born a year after his father's death. His mother, Madam Liu, worked hard to raise him to adulthood. He was intelligent and strong in his youth and became a student at a young age. He read widely and was skilled in literature and art. He was known among his peers for his calligraphy. Zhang Junhengjia, the envoy in charge of education, admired him and selected him to study at the School of Classics, where his studies advanced further. In the Xinmao year of Guangxu, he passed the provincial examination. He was not selected by the Ministry of Rites. He paid for the position of official and was assigned to the Ministry of War. In the Guimao year, he became a Jinshi and remained in the Ministry of War, becoming a secretary in the Department of Military Selection. Soon after, he was granted the title of Advisory Minister of the Bide Academy. Earlier, in the Jiawu year, Duke Liu Zhongcheng led troops to Shanhaiguan to defend against the Japanese pirates. He went to the military headquarters once. After retreating, he joined the public carriage to write a letter, generously presenting his political opinions. His spirit was very strong. When the demon people rioted, he hastily escorted his mother out of the capital. He was immediately robbed. He found a bamboo sedan chair for his mother to sit in and walked with a servant for about forty miles before finding a boat. At that time, his mother cried to him. He smiled to show that he was not suffering and comforted his mother. After returning south to his old residence in Hengyang, he feared the officials and accepted the position of head lecturer at Shigu Academy, also serving at Hanshou Longchi Academy. He originally studied Dai's Rites, the Gongyang Commentary on the Spring and Autumn Annals, and the Zuo Commentary on the Spring and Autumn Annals. His writing and poetry were elegant and discarded the mundane. The students who were taught by him changed their views in response. Later, he served as the director of the Normal School of Law and Politics, the Education Association, the Advisory Bureau, and the Autonomous Bureau. His reputation was high. After the national changes, his mother died at an old age. He was so devastated that he almost gave up his life.

War Horse Double Book of Rites (65) 221

— Master of Seeking Happiness Studio

Eighth Episode: Limitless Sadness and Grievance in Confession, Difficult to Expect Open-Mindedness. Extreme Singing and Dancing, Glimpsing Majesty.

An Yutian loved these teachings, nodding his head like a stubborn stone. He said nothing more, but secretly hardened his heart to go all out. In any case, Liang Xiaoyun was doing this because she truly loved him, and it was the only way to fulfill her wishes and exchange for a future of shared happiness. Although his conscience could not help but feel that his will was weak and that he was not a gentleman, no one would pity or care for a gentleman when he was drifting and impoverished. It was better to be muddleheaded, immersed in a rare gentle village, forgetting those bookish and pedantic thoughts, and just wait for the good news to come from the field of fame and fortune. The next day, he finally saw Mao Deshun arriving in a car to pick them up. As soon as he entered the door, he jumped and bowed to the couple in a military salute, calling them "Sir" and "Madam," flattering them insincerely. Then, he hurriedly spoke about the serious matter, boasting as if he had performed a great service. "I have been paying attention all day. The commander-in-chief is about to leave Beijing in these two days and is very busy. The guests coming to the mansion in the morning and evening are even more eager to take advantage of this urgent time than usual. If Madame An goes to squeeze in with them, I'm afraid there won't be much to talk about. Now there is another good way. The commander-in-chief is definitely going to the Grand Theatre tonight to listen to the great charity performance of all the famous actors. There are more than ten boxes upstairs. The Fifth Madam originally wanted to invite Madam An to listen to the opera together. Why not also invite Sir An to go along? Just go to the theater early. When the commander-in-chief is sitting there feeling a little bored before the good operas start, I will say that I was ordered by the Fifth Madam to lead Sir An to meet him. Taking advantage of his happy mood at that time, you can definitely talk very well. It's getting dark now. Please prepare quickly. First go to the mansion to see the Fifth Madam. Then go to the Grand Theatre together to wait. Although the commander-in-chief also has many dinner appointments in the evening, he will definitely find time to arrive early in order to listen to the good operas. Quick... quick. The car is already waiting at the door. The Fifth Madam especially told me to come and urge you." Liang Xiaoyun was overjoyed. She asked Mao Deshun to rest for a while, then returned to the bedroom to wash and dress up, and instructed An Yutian to also change into a newly made and handsome robe. An Yutian thought to himself that he had really heard so many new tricks these days. There were also special and unexpected ways to see the great and wealthy people of today. You had to go to the theater box, with its mixed sounds of singing and music, to meet them, so that you could catch the commander-in-chief at a happy moment. This was truly mysterious, unfathomable, and profound.

Shanghai Extra Edition of Shen Bao

Talk

The Way of Being a Person 222

— Buddha

What is called the way of being a person? The scope of the way of being a person is very broad. In short, the way of being a person is not to bully others with power or to oppress the weak with strength. You must make things convenient for others and yourself.

The ancients had two sayings: "Do not do what pleases your loved ones but grieves your enemies, and do not do what pleases your enemies but grieves your loved ones." That is, when he is facing a great disaster, or when his coffin is closed, his personality can be judged by these two types of people.

For example, a beggar or someone who is absolutely poor, when they are helpless, there will always be someone to pity or help them. If it is a hooligan or someone with special authority or armed forces, even if this kind of person dies, others will not only not pity them, but will also be happy.

Therefore, there is no absolute standard for the way of being a person, but if this person is beneficial to others in the world, he is a good person; if he is harmful to others, he is an evil person.

Therefore, good people fear their death, and evil people fear that they will not die. When a person reaches the critical point of life and death, the personality of an evil person and a good person can be determined by this. Therefore, just as it is with one person, so it is with a country.

Shanghai Difficulty New Yuefu: Pheasant Flying at Dawn 225

— Meng·Tiao·An·Zhu·

Pheasant flies at dawn, from whence does it fly?

Ten thousand miles of misty sea and Penglai path.

A prodigal son from Penglai travels the sandy battlefield,

Surviving a hundred battles by the river's edge.

Turning his head towards his homeland, tears fall like rain,

Who understands the bitterness of joining the army?

The flying pheasant seems utterly mad,

Military aura dissipates into the light of powder and rouge.

The military gate is a fragrant cave,

Fine wine of grapes sent to the lips.

Three thousand goddesses at one's disposal,

All transformed into the dreams of Yangtai.

Leaving the door, still wearing Five-Shu coins,

Is it Yunsu or rain-like grease, who can tell?

The scenery of a celestial kingdom is truly worthy,

Passersby compete to watch the pheasant flying at dawn.

Science

Wireless Radio 226

— Diao

Of all the modern inventions, none is as astonishing as wireless radio. It transmits the power of electricity through the air for thousands of miles. The saying "Ears that Hear the Wind" has already become a reality. Now, I will explain its principles to the readers.

Electricity can not only flow through metal but also emit a type of wave that travels through the air. The speed of this electrical wave is almost as fast as ordinary light, approximately 300 million meters per second. Electrical waves have different lengths, depending on the storage battery emitting the waves. Some electrical waves have a wavelength of 400 meters, and there are 750,000 waves per second ("300 million divided by 400 equals 750,000"). Therefore, electrical waves differ in wavelength and the number of waves per second.

But how can a receiver receive the electrical waves emitted from a transmitter? This relies on the action of Electric Resonance. What is electric resonance? Electric resonance occurs when a storage battery emits an electrical wave, and another storage battery of the same size, at a considerable distance, is influenced by it and can receive a good electrical wave. This electrical wave becomes an electric current and takes effect within that storage battery. If the storage battery is not the same size, then electric resonance will not occur. We can conduct an experiment using two Leyden Jars placed one foot apart. Use wire to create two square loops and connect them to the tin foil inside and outside the jars. However, one of the wire connections must not be completely secure; leave a small gap. If we pass a very strong electric current through the gap, causing sparks to jump across it, we will find that the wire connected to the other jar also has electricity. Of course, the wire we use should be the same length and thickness and placed parallel to each other.

Since we discovered the action of electric resonance, we have created the wireless telephone and wireless telegraph based on its principles. When a person speaks into a microphone, the varying pitch, length, and continuous nature of their voice affect the microphone, causing it to emit different electrical waves. These electrical waves reach our receiver. As long as we influence the sound-emitting speaker with this electric current and emit different sounds, all these electrical changes follow the pitch and intensity of the person's voice. Therefore, the sounds we hear from the wireless radio are exactly like the person's speech, without any difference.

Stories

Miss 227

— Yunzong

The day before yesterday, I was passing by ×× Road for some errands when I saw my girlfriend, Ying, walking quickly towards me from the opposite direction. She said breathlessly, "Zhu! You've come at the right time! Today, I ran into a 'rascal!'" Her lovely face showed great panic.

"Which one? Where is he?" I asked boldly, showing an attitude of standing up for her. I saw a young man wearing a felt hat and a blue gown behind Ying, turning around and running away.

Ying, still unsettled, pointed at the young man and said, "There! That's him! Oh dear! I was so scared!"

"What happened? Where are you going now?" I continued asking.

"I'm going to school! I came out of my house and was walking to the intersection of ×× Road when suddenly that stranger jumped out from the side and rudely said, 'Miss! I've been thinking about you for a long time!' I was shocked and knew he was no good. I angrily rebuked him, saying, 'Get lost! Be smart!' As I said that, I walked away with big strides, but he still followed closely, saying,

'Ever since our encounter in ×× Lane, I've been unable to forget you, even in my dreams. Today, I see your beautiful face again; it's truly a predestined fate. May I ask for your honorable surname and given name? Where is your fragrant boudoir? How old are you? What school do you attend? Please tell me in detail. We can correspond often and study together. I look forward to it!'

I completely ignored him and just walked silently. But when I walked fast, he also walked fast; when I walked slowly, he also walked slowly. I lost patience and cursed at him, calling him a 'pig'! He still followed closely. I was truly both angry and flustered. Luckily, I ran into you; that 'rascal' finally ran away. If you hadn't come, I would have suffered another moment of tormented entanglement!" After she finished speaking, she seemed somewhat embarrassed.

I said with a smile, "This is the 'Miss's' difficulty in walking the road!"

Street Corner News

On Avenue Joffre 228

— Ding Nu

On the Avenue Joffre, which is full of exotic flavors, my friend recently discovered a secret. I thought that many people might not know this secret, so let me reveal it here.

The truth is this: one afternoon during a drunken spring breeze, my friend was returning from the Lower Park. At a bus stop, he boarded a tram. At this time, people were crowding together. Coincidentally, a foreign young woman squeezed in front of my friend. Her hair was curled, her lips were painted with lipstick, and she wore a fitted red dress, floating like a fairy. The tram sped forward, and the sensual scent wafted from the young woman's side, making my friend feel intoxicated. The season was spring, and the person standing in front of him was also a spring character, so my friend naturally had to let the fragrance of spring intoxicate his senses.

My friend just stood there blankly, not caring that the foreign young woman's head was leaning against his chest. My friend didn't notice what the young woman did afterward at all.

Only once, his hat seemed to touch something. He focused and looked back to see that next to him stood a foreign man. Anyone could tell at a glance which country these people came from. Although they had a country, their country did not accept them. These were the White Russians we are familiar with. At the time, my friend didn't think it was a big deal. After one glance, he stood still in his original position until the young woman got off the tram. Only then did he turn around as if he had lost something and sat down in the car.

When he returned home and touched his pocket, his wallet was gone. He was stunned and then understood what the young woman's intimacy just now meant.

Random Chatter

He Cried 229

— Leng Mang

The purpose of going to an entertainment venue is for everyone to find some joy because they are too bored from working or studying every day! However, the reality is often not like that.

One day, my friend was very happy and knew I was very poor, so he invited me to see a movie and also invited several Misses. We entered a relatively large movie theater. The movie had already started a few minutes before, so we all found our seats in the dark, following the direction of the usher's flashlight.

At this time, everyone was silent, watching the movie unfold scene by scene. At the same time, a Miss who was very fluent in English was reading the words on the screen.

Suddenly, after a while, two Misses behind me started crying. We all looked back in surprise. My friend asked what was wrong.

One of the ladies said, "Ah! It turns out there is a sentimental Miss who sympathizes with the sadness in the movie! That's why she's crying."

At that time, I thought that there are many people in the world who shed tears over books, but in my opinion, the plot of this movie was not very good. There were one or two scenes that were a bit tense, which only made me freeze for a while. Ultimately, it wasn't worth crying over. Therefore, I discovered that women are indeed softer than men.

Zhang Shouchun versus Zhu Huisheng, rent and return of house case: The defendant shall pay the plaintiff two hundred and seventy-five yuan in rent. The plaintiff's remaining claims and application for provisional execution are dismissed. The plaintiff shall bear one-third of the litigation costs, and the defendant shall bear two-thirds.

Fengtai Company versus Qian Lianyi et al., rent and return of house case: The defendants Qian Lianyi and Tao Taoniang shall each pay the plaintiff one hundred and thirty-one yuan in rent and eighteen cents in street cleaning fees. The plaintiff's remaining claims and application for provisional execution are dismissed. The plaintiff shall bear one-fifth of the litigation costs, and the defendants shall bear the remainder equally.

Mo Yueying et al. versus Mo Liansheng, revocation of sale case: The plaintiff's lawsuit is dismissed. The plaintiff shall bear the litigation costs.

Lixing Foreign Firm versus Luo Ping, debt case: The defendant shall repay the plaintiff one thousand two hundred and forty-two yuan, five jiao, and four fen, plus interest at an annual rate of five percent from the date of the lawsuit until the date of full payment. The defendant shall bear the litigation costs.

Baolu Maizhinan versus Bai Ligao, debt appeal case: The appeal is dismissed. The appellant shall bear the second instance litigation costs.

Cai Jicai versus Zhu Yufeng et al., debt case: The defendant Zhu Yufeng shall repay the plaintiff one hundred and twenty-eight yuan. If execution is ineffective, the guarantor Gao Defa shall pay on his behalf. The defendant Zhu Yufeng shall bear the litigation costs.

Yihe Company, Yao Youxuan versus Ni Gulian et al., rent arrears case: The defendant Ni Gulian shall pay the plaintiff eighteen yuan and three jiao in rent. Wang Fuqing shall pay the plaintiff seventy-two yuan and twelve jiao in rent. Xu Huating shall pay the plaintiff one hundred and fifty-seven yuan and twenty-four jiao in rent. The defendants shall bear the litigation costs in proportion to their rent arrears.

Aigao Foreign Firm versus Zhuang Da, loan case: The plaintiff's lawsuit is dismissed. The plaintiff shall bear the litigation costs.

Ruihua Company versus Chen Yuji, rent arrears case: The defendant shall pay the plaintiff four hundred and fifty-six yuan in rent. The plaintiff's remaining claims are dismissed. The defendant shall bear the litigation costs.

Huikang et al. versus Xia Guifang, rent reduction case: The plaintiff's lawsuit is dismissed. The plaintiff shall bear the litigation costs.

Heji Educational Supplies Store versus Tianzhang Paper Store, goods payment case: The defendant Tianzhang Paper Store shall repay the plaintiff two hundred and thirteen yuan and six jiao and two fen. If execution is ineffective, Xia Ziqiu shall pay on its behalf. The defendants shall jointly bear the litigation costs.

Xin Ruihe Foreign Firm, Yang Jianmei versus Gong Anren, rent arrears case: The defendant shall pay the plaintiff one hundred and ninety yuan. The plaintiff's remaining claims are dismissed. The defendant shall bear six-tenths of the litigation costs, and the plaintiff shall bear four-tenths.

Wu Jue versus Jiang Yichuan, rent arrears and eviction case: The defendants shall each pay the plaintiff fifty-one yuan and twelve cents in rent. The plaintiff's remaining claims are dismissed. The defendants shall bear two-thirds of the litigation costs, and the plaintiff shall bear one-third.

Xie Pingfeng versus Yuan Fengming, rent arrears and eviction case: The defendant shall pay the plaintiff four hundred and eighty yuan in rent. The plaintiff's remaining claims are dismissed. The defendant shall bear two-thirds of the litigation costs, and the plaintiff shall bear one-third.

Jin Yuanru versus Taifeng Factory, promissory note case: The defendant shall pay the plaintiff two hundred yuan for the promissory note and overdue interest at an annual rate of five percent from June 30, 1931, until the date of execution. The defendant shall bear the litigation costs.

Ruihua Company versus Chen Zhaoxiang, rent and return of house case: The defendant shall pay the plaintiff two hundred and eighty yuan in rent. The plaintiff's remaining claims are dismissed. The plaintiff shall bear one-third of the litigation costs, and the defendant shall bear two-thirds. The plaintiff in this case may seek provisional execution after providing a security deposit of eighty yuan. (Above, May 26)

Civil Judgement:

Lei Chunsheng vs. Xu Baojin, housing rent case: The defendant shall pay the plaintiff housing rent of one hundred and two yuan. Litigation costs, except for the settlement part of seven-tenths to be resolved separately and the withdrawn part of one-tenth to be borne by the plaintiff, the remaining two-tenths shall be borne by the defendant.

Mai Shasheng vs. Tang Agen, loan case: The plaintiff's lawsuit is dismissed. The plaintiff shall bear the litigation costs.

Chen Ruiqing vs. Shao Zhongheng, guarantee debt case: The defendant shall repay the plaintiff the sum of 12,480.25 yuan for goods from the Yongchengtai business managed by the plaintiff, plus statutory interest at an annual rate of five percent from November 17, 1931, until the date of execution. The defendant shall bear the litigation costs.

Xi Caishi vs. Xi Wushi, price difference appeal case: The appeal is dismissed. The appellant shall bear the second instance litigation costs.

Yu Fenggen vs. Tan Xinhua, rent arrears case: The defendant shall repay the plaintiff housing rent of one hundred and eighty-three yuan. The defendant shall bear the litigation costs.
